 \Hypertarget{classqiskit_1_1circuit_1_1quantumcircuit_1_1_quantum_circuit_ad225b3681d8f8ee758b7da21cf6531b8_ad225b3681d8f8ee758b7da21cf6531b8}\index{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit@{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit}!tensor@{tensor}}
\index{tensor@{tensor}!qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit@{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{tensor()}{tensor()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classqiskit_1_1circuit_1_1quantumcircuit_1_1_quantum_circuit_ad225b3681d8f8ee758b7da21cf6531b8_ad225b3681d8f8ee758b7da21cf6531b8} 
 Optional\mbox{[}"{}Quantum\+Circuit"{}\mbox{]} qiskit.\+circuit.\+quantumcircuit.\+Quantum\+Circuit.\+tensor (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{"{}Quantum\+Circuit"{}}]{other}{, }\item[{bool }]{inplace}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Tensor ``self`` with ``other``.

Remember that in the little-endian convention the leftmost operation will be at the bottom
of the circuit. See also
`the docs <https://docs.quantum.ibm.com/guides/construct-circuits>`__
for more information.

.. code-block:: text

         ┌────────┐        ┌─────┐          ┌─────┐
    q_0: ┤ bottom ├ ⊗ q_0: ┤ top ├  = q_0: ─┤ top ├──
         └────────┘        └─────┘         ┌┴─────┴─┐
                                      q_1: ┤ bottom ├
                                           └────────┘

Args:
    other (QuantumCircuit): The other circuit to tensor this circuit with.
    inplace (bool): If ``True``, modify the object. Otherwise return composed circuit.

Examples:

    .. plot::
       :alt: Circuit diagram output by the previous code.
       :include-source:

       from qiskit import QuantumCircuit
       top = QuantumCircuit(1)
       top.x(0);
       bottom = QuantumCircuit(2)
       bottom.cry(0.2, 0, 1);
       tensored = bottom.tensor(top)
       tensored.draw('mpl')

Returns:
    QuantumCircuit: The tensored circuit (returns ``None`` if ``inplace=True``).
\end{DoxyVerb}
 \Hypertarget{classqiskit_1_1circuit_1_1quantumcircuit_1_1_quantum_circuit_a24408dc9fe661698477622e85ab62578_a24408dc9fe661698477622e85ab62578}\index{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit@{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit}!to\_gate@{to\_gate}}
\index{to\_gate@{to\_gate}!qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit@{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit}}

 \mbox{\hyperlink{classqiskit_1_1circuit_1_1gate_1_1_gate}{Gate}} qiskit.\+circuit.\+quantumcircuit.\+Quantum\+Circuit.\+to\+\_\+gate (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{dict\mbox{[}\mbox{\hyperlink{classqiskit_1_1circuit_1_1parameter_1_1_parameter}{Parameter}}, Parameter\+Value\+Type\mbox{]} \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} None }]{parameter\+\_\+map}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{str \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} None }]{label}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Create a :class:`.Gate` out of this circuit.  The circuit must act only qubits and
contain only unitary operations.

.. seealso::
    :func:`circuit_to_gate`
        The underlying driver of this method.

Args:
    parameter_map: For parameterized circuits, a mapping from parameters in the circuit to
        parameters to be used in the gate. If ``None``, existing circuit parameters will
        also parameterize the gate.
    label : Optional gate label.

Returns:
    Gate: a composite gate encapsulating this circuit (can be decomposed back).
\end{DoxyVerb}

 \Hypertarget{classqiskit_1_1circuit_1_1quantumcircuit_1_1_quantum_circuit_a6ef89efa8f25e7514f9183dd897ebf02_a6ef89efa8f25e7514f9183dd897ebf02}\index{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit@{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit}!unitary@{unitary}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{unitary()}{unitary()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classqiskit_1_1circuit_1_1quantumcircuit_1_1_quantum_circuit_a6ef89efa8f25e7514f9183dd897ebf02_a6ef89efa8f25e7514f9183dd897ebf02} 
qiskit.\+circuit.\+quantumcircuit.\+Quantum\+Circuit.\+unitary (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{np.\+ndarray \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} \mbox{\hyperlink{classqiskit_1_1circuit_1_1gate_1_1_gate}{Gate}} \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} \mbox{\hyperlink{classqiskit_1_1quantum__info_1_1operators_1_1base__operator_1_1_base_operator}{Base\+Operator}}}]{obj}{, }\item[{Sequence\mbox{[}Qubit\+Specifier\mbox{]}}]{qubits}{, }\item[{str \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} None }]{label}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Apply unitary gate specified by ``obj`` to ``qubits``.

Args:
    obj: Unitary operator.
    qubits: The circuit qubits to apply the transformation to.
    label: Unitary name for backend [Default: None].

Returns:
    QuantumCircuit: The quantum circuit.

Example:

    Apply a gate specified by a unitary matrix to a quantum circuit

    .. code-block:: python

        from qiskit import QuantumCircuit
        matrix = [[0, 0, 0, 1],
                [0, 0, 1, 0],
                [1, 0, 0, 0],
                [0, 1, 0, 0]]
        circuit = QuantumCircuit(2)
        circuit.unitary(matrix, [0, 1])
\end{DoxyVerb}
 \Hypertarget{classqiskit_1_1circuit_1_1quantumcircuit_1_1_quantum_circuit_a885eb36a8611a7354a7f770cc634460a_a885eb36a8611a7354a7f770cc634460a}\index{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit@{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit}!while\_loop@{while\_loop}}
\index{while\_loop@{while\_loop}!qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit@{qiskit.circuit.quantumcircuit.QuantumCircuit}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{while\_loop()}{while\_loop()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classqiskit_1_1circuit_1_1quantumcircuit_1_1_quantum_circuit_a885eb36a8611a7354a7f770cc634460a_a885eb36a8611a7354a7f770cc634460a} 
qiskit.\+circuit.\+quantumcircuit.\+Quantum\+Circuit.\+while\+\_\+loop (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{condition}{, }\item[{}]{body}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{qubits}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{clbits}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{}]{label}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Create a ``while`` loop on this circuit.

There are two forms for calling this function.  If called with all its arguments (with the
possible exception of ``label``), it will create a
:obj:`~qiskit.circuit.controlflow.WhileLoopOp` with the given ``body``.  If ``body`` (and
``qubits`` and ``clbits``) are *not* passed, then this acts as a context manager, which
will automatically build a :obj:`~qiskit.circuit.controlflow.WhileLoopOp` when the scope
finishes.  In this form, you do not need to keep track of the qubits or clbits you are
using, because the scope will handle it for you.

Example usage::

    from qiskit.circuit import QuantumCircuit, Clbit, Qubit
    bits = [Qubit(), Qubit(), Clbit()]
    qc = QuantumCircuit(bits)

    with qc.while_loop((bits[2], 0)):
        qc.h(0)
        qc.cx(0, 1)
        qc.measure(0, 0)

Args:
    condition (Tuple[Union[ClassicalRegister, Clbit], int]): An equality condition to be
        checked prior to executing ``body``. The left-hand side of the condition must be a
        :obj:`~ClassicalRegister` or a :obj:`~Clbit`, and the right-hand side must be an
        integer or boolean.
    body (Optional[QuantumCircuit]): The loop body to be repeatedly executed.  Omit this to
        use the context-manager mode.
    qubits (Optional[Sequence[Qubit]]): The circuit qubits over which the loop body should
        be run.  Omit this to use the context-manager mode.
    clbits (Optional[Sequence[Clbit]]): The circuit clbits over which the loop body should
        be run.  Omit this to use the context-manager mode.
    label (Optional[str]): The string label of the instruction in the circuit.

Returns:
    InstructionSet or WhileLoopContext: If used in context-manager mode, then this should be
    used as a ``with`` resource, which will infer the block content and operands on exit.
    If the full form is used, then this returns a handle to the instructions created.

Raises:
    CircuitError: if an incorrect calling convention is used.
\end{DoxyVerb}
